The proof lets the common direction hold the connections together. What becomes available is direction-family structure: a way to organize same-bearing connections for later extension, transport, and coordinate audit. The family remains source-bound because only connections with the preserved direction may enter it.

Theorem 324 — Three Direction Families Exposed

Claim: The sixfold boundary exposes three recurring direction families.

The sixfold boundary now exposes three recurring direction families. Selected station connections repeat their bearings in three native ways, and those repetitions organize the field. The proof does not borrow a grid or a theory of parallel classes. It reads what the closed six-station boundary and its connections make visible. What becomes available is the three-family direction scaffold, the native directional order from which later field extension and coordinate audit can begin.

Theorem 325 — Direction-Family Evidence Available

Claim: Direction-family evidence is available in the constructed substrate.

The direction-family work closes by making its evidence available. The constructed substrate contains selected station connections, repeated bearings, and three direction families exposed by the sixfold boundary. This does not yet authorize every theorem about lines, parallels, or coordinates. It provides the evidence those later readings must spend. What stands is direction-family availability: the field can now carry, extend, and audit directions because their recurrence has been earned inside the construction itself.

Theorem 326 — Repeated Triangular Field Availability

Claim: A repeated triangular field is available from extended direction families.

The extended direction families now yield more than isolated recurrence. Their crossings produce repeatable stations, their joins form local triangular cells, and shared sides let those cells stand beside one another. The proof therefore gathers the outward spread into a repeated triangular field. This is not a borrowed tessellation theorem and not a coordinate grid disguised as construction. It is the field produced when the three recurring direction families continue to meet under preserved relations. What becomes available is a repeated triangular substrate, broad enough for transport and audit while still answerable to the fixed-opening source that made the first cell lawful.

Theorem 327 — Local Relation Inside One Cell

Claim: A local relation may appear inside one triangular cell.

The repeated field can now be inspected locally. Inside one triangular cell, stations, sides, and direction-family joins may supply a relation that was not being claimed for the whole field at once. The proof permits the relation to appear where its own cell has actually provided the necessary evidence. This is a narrowing move, not a generalization. The field is large, but the claim begins in one cell. What becomes available is local relation evidence: a relation may stand inside a triangular cell when that cell supplies the defining station and side conditions.

Theorem 328 — Another Cell Preserves Same Structure

Claim: Another triangular cell may preserve the same relevant structure.

A second triangular cell may now be compared with the first, but only through structure. The proof does not say that the second cell is useful because it looks similar. It asks whether the relevant stations, sides, and direction-family roles are preserved there. When those conditions remain intact, the second cell can carry the same kind of local structure. What becomes available is a possible companion cell for inspection. What remains refused is visual analogy without preservation, because the proof field can reuse only what the construction has kept alive.

Theorem 329 — Inspection in Other Cell

Claim: The preserved structure allows the local relation to be inspected in the other cell.

When the second cell preserves the relevant structure, the local relation from the first cell can be inspected there. The proof does not yet say the relation has been freely copied across the field. It says the other cell contains the conditions that made the relation meaningful, so the relation can be checked again under those conditions. This gives transport its first working motion in the repeated field: local evidence can be inspected elsewhere when the structure is preserved. The permission lands as inspection under preserved conditions, not as unbounded repetition.

Theorem 330 — Reuse Requires Defining Conditions

Claim: The relation is reused only when its defining conditions are preserved.

The proof now states the rule that controls reuse. A relation does not travel because a later sentence wants it, and it does not travel because another picture resembles the first. It travels only when the defining conditions that made it true are preserved. Station roles, side witnesses, direction-family placement, or shared-cell structure must remain available. What becomes available is lawful reuse. What is refused is silent copying. The theorem gives the repeated field power without loosening the source boundary: reuse is allowed, but only with its receipt.

Theorem 331 — Reuse Without New Opening

Claim: The reuse does not depend on a new compass opening.

Once the defining conditions are preserved, relation reuse does not require a new compass opening. The original fixed opening remains the root measure, and the repeated field carries its consequences through direction families and cell structure. The proof therefore avoids multiplying sources. A relation may reappear because its conditions survive, not because a fresh measuring act has been smuggled in. What becomes available is reuse under the old source authority. The fixed opening is not replaced; it is remembered through the relations it has already generated.

Theorem 332 — Reuse Without Coordinate Generation

Claim: The reuse does not depend on coordinate generation.

Reuse also does not depend on coordinates creating the field. A coordinate record may later check a repeated station or compare a relation, but it is not the engine of reuse. The repeated triangular cell, the preserved station roles, and the direction-family structure do the constructional work. The proof again keeps audit below source. What becomes available is coordinate-free transport of preserved relations, with coordinates admitted only afterward as memory or verification. This protects the field from letting its bookkeeping pretend to be its birth.

Theorem 333 — Transportability for Preserved Local Relations

Claim: Transportability is available for preserved local relations.

The previous refusals now gather into a positive permission. A local relation may travel through the repeated triangular field when the construction preserves the conditions that define it. It does not need a new compass opening, and it does not arise from coordinate generation. It needs the relevant station, side, direction, or cell relations to remain intact. What crystallises is transportability for preserved local relations. The field can now carry earned facts from one lawful cell to another, while resemblance, convenience, and analytic shortcuts stay outside the gate.

Theorem 334 — Constructed Figure After Source Operations

Claim: A constructed figure is present only after source operations have produced stations, steps, cells, closure, direction, or transportable relations.

The book now tightens the word figure. A constructed figure is not whatever appears on the page. It is present only where source operations have produced the relations that make it count: stations, steps, cells, closure, direction families, or transportable relations. The proof refuses the temptation to treat sight as source. A visible form may invite attention, but constructional history gives it proof value. What becomes available is a disciplined figure standard. Later geometry may use figures, but only figures whose parts have been earned.

Theorem 335 — Visual Feature Not Enough

Claim: A visual feature is not enough to count as proof.

A visual feature by itself cannot carry proof. A line may look straight, a pair may look equal, a crossing may look centered, but appearance does not preserve the source relation. The theorem refuses diagrammatic persuasion unless the feature is tied back to construction. This is not hostility to the visible figure; it is the condition under which the visible figure becomes trustworthy. What becomes available is a refusal-test for every later claim: if the feature is only seen and not earned, it cannot yet stand as proof.

Theorem 336 — Claimed Relation Needs Source

Claim: A claimed relation must be tied to an earned source relation.

Every claimed relation now faces the same demand. It must be tied to an earned source relation before the proof can spend it. The tie may run through fixed opening, boundary generation, station selection, stepping, cell formation, closure, direction recurrence, transport, or audit after construction. Without such a tie, the claim is only a sentence. With it, the sentence can land. What becomes available is source-tethered relation language. What remains refused is any free relation asserted because it would be useful downstream.

Theorem 337 — Equal-Side Claims Need Equal Opening

Claim: Equal-side claims must be tied to equal-opening evidence.

An equal-side claim may now be made only by returning to equal-opening evidence. The proof does not let equality enter as a general school category. A side is equal in this source-relevant sense when the same fixed opening witnesses the relevant reaches or steps. If that witness is missing, the equal-side claim has not been paid for. What becomes available is an equality filter for sides: equal-opening evidence licenses the claim; visual matching does not. Later cells and figures must answer to that evidence before using equal-side language.

Theorem 338 — Boundary Claims Need Fixed Sweep

Claim: Boundary claims must be tied to fixed-sweep generation.

Boundary language must remember its source. A boundary counts here because a fixed compass opening was swept from a selected center, leaving reached positions under one center-bound relation. A later claim about a boundary must therefore point back to fixed-sweep generation or to a transported condition that lawfully preserves it. The proof refuses generic curve language. What becomes available is source-bound boundary use: boundary claims may stand where the fixed sweep or its earned local analogue supplies the relation.

Theorem 339 — Station Claims Need Selection

Claim: Station claims must be tied to selected station availability.

Stationhood is now placed under its own discipline. A point is not a station merely because it is visible. It becomes a station when the construction selects it, generates it by direction-family crossing, or preserves a role that allows it to support later action. The proof therefore ties station claims to selected station availability. What becomes available is controlled station language throughout the growing field. What remains refused is any claim that a visible mark can act without having first received station authority.

Theorem 340 — Step Claims Need Fixed Opening

Claim: Step claims must be tied to fixed-opening boundary stepping.

A step claim must be tied to the fixed-opening step that earned stepping in the first place. Adjacent boundary stations were joined by one preserved opening, and repeated local steps carry authority only through that relation or a preserved transport of it. The proof refuses to call any short segment a step just because it looks like one. What becomes available is step language under measure witness. A step may be spent when fixed-opening evidence supplies it; otherwise the word remains unavailable.

Theorem 341 — Cell Claims Need Station Pairs

Claim: Cell claims must be tied to supplied station-pair relations.

A cell claim must show its station-pair relations. Three stations do not become a triangular cell just by sitting near one another. The joins among them must be supplied, and the side relations that bound the cell must be available. The proof therefore returns every cell claim to its pairwise evidence. What becomes available is cellhood with a receipt: a cell stands when its station pairs are lawfully held. This protects later assemblies from treating any visible cluster as proof-bearing.

Theorem 342 — Closure Claims Need Six-Step Return

Claim: Closure claims must be tied to six-step return evidence.

Closure is not a feeling of completeness. In this source field, first closure was earned by six equal-opening boundary steps returning to the starting station. Any later claim of closure must therefore identify the return or the preserved structure that supplies it. The proof refuses to confuse a finished-looking drawing with a closed construction. What becomes available is return-based closure language. Closure may be spent where the source walk has come back to its beginning; otherwise the demand remains open.

Theorem 343 — Transported Claims Need Preserved Conditions

Claim: Transported claims must be tied to preservation of defining conditions.

A transported claim must bring its conditions with it. The proof does not allow a result to leap from one cell to another without the station roles, side relations, direction-family structure, or audit conditions that defined it. Transport is therefore a preservation event, not a copying event. What becomes available is a rule for later movement through the field: carried claims must carry their defining conditions. Anything less is resemblance, and resemblance is not proof.

Theorem 344 — Proof-Bearing Figure

Claim: A figure becomes proof-bearing only when construction has forced the relation it claims.

The figure can now be trusted only where construction has forced the relation it claims. A drawn form may guide attention, but it becomes proof-bearing when the underlying operations have made its stations, sides, closure, direction, or transport relations stand. This theorem gathers the previous filters into one standard. What becomes available is proof-bearing figurehood: the visible form may participate in proof when its claim is backed by source operations. What remains refused is the old habit of letting a diagram prove by looking right.

Theorem 345 — Sixfold Boundary Closure Earned

Claim: Sixfold boundary closure has been earned.

The proof now returns to the sixfold source and names what has been earned. Boundary stepping under the fixed opening has produced a six-step return to the starting station. What stands is sixfold boundary closure: a completed source circuit that can support central cell count, half-turn reading, and later connector work without importing polygon theory.

Claim: Six adjacent boundary-station pairs are available after closure.

After sixfold closure, the ordered boundary cycle supplies six adjacent pairs. Each pair is defined by successive stations in the equal-opening walk. What becomes available is a register of six boundary-station pairs, each ready to form a central cell with the center. The six central cells now share a common center. Each cell uses the center and one adjacent boundary pair, so the cells occur in order around that source station. What becomes available is around-center meeting of the six cells, the immediate shape of the turn field before any degree language has appeared.

It then lets a non-preserving change breaks the source constraint, so that preserved equality keeps the original relation intact. The paragraph keeps the fused architecture honest: geometry holds the constructed figure, trigonometry reads stable ratio only where earned, coordinate geometry audits position, and algebra records preserved relation without taking over the source. The final movement is that the transformed form remains proof memory of the same relation. What becomes available is later algebra may remain source-bound. The theorem therefore advances the finish without pretending that completion licenses any unearned shortcut.

Appendices and Glossary

The appendices appear here in the shell so the book has its reference apparatus from the beginning. Later drafts can move these to the back, but keeping them visible during composition protects the paragraph writing from drift.

Appendix A — Canonical Paragraph Stencil

Each readable block paragraph should silently preserve this structure:

[Block ID] — [Title]. The claim asks for [target permission] to stand. The proof begins by [first movement], then [middle movement], then [refusal, preservation, expansion, integration, or closure]. As the sentences contract, [dominant operator pattern] does the main work: [brief axes movement]. The block lands by making [new affordance] available while refusing [unearned import]. From here, later proof may spend [permission] but may not yet spend [forbidden stronger claim].

The paragraph should not become a miniature essay. It should make the block readable while preserving proof pressure.

Appendix B — Sentence-Walk Receipt

1. SentenceQuote exactly. Do not paraphrase before classification.
2. AxesOperator · Orientation · Remainder.
3. Contraction nameFixed name from the 54-cell table. Do not localize, rename, or improve it case by case.
4. Ultra-short formFixed X-Y form from the lookup table.
5. CrystallisationOne compact sentence showing how this exact sentence contracts into the fixed cell: Operator does the work; Orientation gives the direction of resolution; Remainder names what is left standing.
6. LandingOne sentence saying what is now allowed, refused, preserved, completed, or made stand.

Appendix C — Axis Glossary

Operators

Distinction places, bounds, selects, excludes, narrows, assigns, or fixes something as this rather than that.

Expansion opens reach, field, spread, multiplicity, continuation, or outward availability.

Relation maintains bearing between terms, roles, positions, conditions, or patterns.

Correction revises, redirects, repairs, reweights, cancels, or replaces a live prior reading.

Integration organizes parts into one functional arrangement, system, body, field, or unit.

Closure satisfies a live local demand, validates, preserves, exhausts, or brings continuation to rest.

Orientations

Toward is focal convergence into a target, formed unit, role, product, placement, or state.

Across is retained span across terms, levels, comparisons, dependencies, routes, or repeated cases.

Away is release from a prior frame, false source, dependency, threat, confinement, or rejected path.

Remainders

Is leaves a standing condition, status, identity, role, fact, availability, or fixedness.

With leaves held bearing: dependency, pairing, correspondence, balance, support, shared pattern, or mutual reference.

Does leaves an enacted outcome: operation, production, transformation, field generation, structure formation, completion, or event.

Use the contraction name as the fixed stack-gathering handle. Local nuance belongs in crystallisation and landing.

Appendix E — Main-Body Block Template

<article class="block" id="theorem-001"> <h3>Theorem 001 — Preserved Compass Opening</h3> <p class="claim"><strong>Claim:</strong> One compass opening is preserved through the construction.</p> <p>[Completed readable paragraph goes here.]</p> </article>

Appendix F — Editorial Rules for Appending

One block, one paragraph. The paragraph may mention the claim, the proof movement, the dominant contractions, the crystallised permission, and the refusal. It should not become a full table.

No local renaming. If contraction names are mentioned, use the fixed names from Appendix D.

No unearned branch language. Geometry, trigonometry, coordinate geometry, and algebra appear only when their source permissions have been made active.

End in permission or refusal. Each paragraph should leave the reader knowing what the block now allows and what it still does not allow.
